  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_22504365-1909-4e06-a540-f793c9dee188'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    };

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/20967960-alexander-marinov">Alexander Marinov</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Actually I find it interesting. Usually the reader knows the whole background of the story. Or, at least, he knows much more than the characters in th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Actually I find it interesting. Usually the reader knows the whole background of the story. Or, at least, he knows much more than the characters in the book. In "Cell" the reader knows as little as the characters - pretty much nothing. I was feeling like a member of the company, not knowing what the big picture is, how strong the enemy actually is. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4084863721341219105">Focusing on one main plot element can go wrong if the writer is no plotter and doesn´t construct a finetuned metaplot around the fictional device.<br/><br/>Without the extreme problem of the suspension of disbelief, especially after the first half of the book, it would be the used interesting characterization with some horror elements, but it´s a bit Sci-Fi and dystopia too, and that ruins the whole thing.   <span id="freeText4084863721341219105" style="display:none">Focusing on one main plot element can go wrong if the writer is no plotter and doesn´t construct a finetuned metaplot around the fictional device.<br /><br />Without the extreme problem of the suspension of disbelief, especially after the first half of the book, it would be the used interesting characterization with some horror elements, but it´s a bit Sci-Fi and dystopia too, and that ruins the whole thing. Similar to Langoliers, King can´t deal with these things and for any reason, this can even be felt in the parts that have no techno elements integrated. It´s a bit as if subconscious discomfort and nervosity reduce the quality of his writing, a curse, a quantum parasite not wanting that he tells us the truth about the universe. Stupid aliens.<br /><br />King had the idea to write something with this fancy new smartphones and thought it could be mixed up with some dystopian nightmare, psi stuff, survival elements, but it just doesn´t ignite, never! It´s everything, the characters behave unreliably, the explanations for how and why it happens are ridiculous, how the plot continues and finishes is …, yuck, just don´t read it. <br /><br />I´ve not read Cujo because of the bad reviews (sadly read this one before focusing on meta scores), but at least he doesn´t remember writing it because of being wasted and I see no similar explanation, excuse, or whatever in this case. <br /><br />Could also be possible that he was so invested in writing Lisey´s story that was published the same year and has personal elements in it, that he just didn´t really care about the quality of this one. It´s a special irony, because his The Stand is the masterpiece of apocalyptic literature, possibly the best one ever written, which makes this one look even worse and unnecessary. The, meanwhile, first and only derision of fans too because I can´t believe that he didn´t notice that there is something wrong here. What I did especially notice is that it´s quite interesting before the chaos breaks out and everything worsens afterward, as if King would have started cheerfully and thought after a while, whatever, I´ll just finish this one without love for the art.<br /><br />I deemed it impossible, but this is a bad King book, not fangirled/boyed readers who don´t like the writing style so much might even give it a 2 star rating.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/Cell">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>

<div id="review_2597668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597668" />
    <a title="Leah Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/165114-leah-williams"><img alt="Leah Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596534455p2/165114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2597668?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah Williams" href="/user/show/165114-leah-williams">Leah Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1850503546278924073">Literary critics can moan all they want about Stephen King's "penny dreadful" oeuvre, but his mastery at the craft of storytelling is indisputable. King writes his novels like a seduction, the story unfolding delicately and deliberately. As any Stephen King fan knows, his coy expository chapters often take up the first hundred pages or more. In Cell, however, the reader is brutally dragged into the main action--unspeakable, senseless violence--within the first seven pages. Cell is by far King's </span>
  <span id="freeText1850503546278924073" style="display:none">Literary critics can moan all they want about Stephen King's "penny dreadful" oeuvre, but his mastery at the craft of storytelling is indisputable. King writes his novels like a seduction, the story unfolding delicately and deliberately. As any Stephen King fan knows, his coy expository chapters often take up the first hundred pages or more. In Cell, however, the reader is brutally dragged into the main action--unspeakable, senseless violence--within the first seven pages. Cell is by far King's most brutal, transgressive work to date.<br /><br />Many have compared Cell to his earlier epic, The Stand. On the surface, the novels are quite similar: an apocolyptic event threatens the very existence of the human race as a band of survivors struggle to come to terms with the carnage and avert further catastrophe. Cell, however, is the far more mature novel of the pair. The Stand was, in many ways, a novel by an idealistic youth, whereas Cell is filled with the trenchant and world-weary observations of an adult. The subtext is laden with so much chillingly apt futurist rhetoric that it is as though the author had Marshall McLuhan whispering plot devices and metaphors into his ear as he labored over his typewriter. King manages to explore several of the major sociocultural conflicts of our time, most persuasively the end of the era of individualism and the rise of collectivism, here symptomatic of heavy reliance on technology. Whereas many dystopian novels are almost comically blunt when expounding upon the dangers of collectivism, King's horrific plot and action give his metaphors a sort of subtlety that renders his subtext much more graceful and easier to stomach than the work of Ayn Rand.<br /><br />As the epigraphs indicate, it is also a meditation on the intrinsic violence of the human race. King clearly feels as though the world is out of control and wants to find out why. His preferred genre, horror, is an excellent one with which to consider the depravaties of modern life. The Stand was a novel that, if not upbeat, was at least optimistic--a reflection of the times in which it was written. There was also violence, but it had its own biblical logic, if violence can ever be called logical. In Cell, the violence is senseless, oppressive, and omnipresent. There seems to be little promise for a better world... at least not one inhabited by human beings.<br /><br />Many reviewers took issue with the unresolved ending. Considering the subtext of the novel, however, the reader will find that the ending's abruptness actually informs the sense that Cell, besides being an excellent horror yarn, is a meticulously painted portrait of the horrors of global culture. The many crises of our time are still developing and mutating. The end is not yet, it seems, in sight.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1850503546278924073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_574639582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574639582" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4643325-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535048395p2/4643325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574639582?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/4643325-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4643325-paul?shelf=end-of-world-dystopian-apocalyptic">end-of-world-dystopian-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574639582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4267605139476213511">I suddenly realised half way through this book that it is really a zombie novel. After a shower I felt better and rationalised that this was occupying my "wouldn't normally read this" slot in my book consumption; sigh of relief. <br/>I must admit that I did enjoy some of King's early novels, but this was so far fetched and ridiculous (Am I really saying "It" wasn't?). The plot is simple. Somehow, someone sends a pulse through the mobile phone system which wipes clean a person's mind and sends them ba</span>
  <span id="freeText4267605139476213511" style="display:none">I suddenly realised half way through this book that it is really a zombie novel. After a shower I felt better and rationalised that this was occupying my "wouldn't normally read this" slot in my book consumption; sigh of relief. <br />I must admit that I did enjoy some of King's early novels, but this was so far fetched and ridiculous (Am I really saying "It" wasn't?). The plot is simple. Somehow, someone sends a pulse through the mobile phone system which wipes clean a person's mind and sends them back to basics and they become unreasoning killers. Those that survive the bloodbath begin to flock together and develop a sort of telepathy. Meanwhile those that didn't hear the pulse and survived the bloodbath also group together and a struggle for survival begins. <br />Sometimes books like this are good mindless fun and I do enjoy well written thrillers. King does write well and is a natural storyteller; but there is something insidious at the heart of this. Basically (and this is actually said in the book), when everything is stripped away from men and women; what is left - MURDER. This, quite simply, is the Doctrine of The Fall (not Mark E Smith's rather good Manchester band), as found in the Old Testament. We are born in sin and are wicked at heart; our first instincts being to kill rather than care for each other. That is the problem with this book; that premise. Nature and nurture matter not; we are hard-wired to Murder. <br />In my more depressive moments I realise we have created an economic system which destroys the weak and poor rather well and we regularly elect governments that play and build on xenophobia and the evils of those who are different. However, in my heart I believe we all have that spark that would rather care for others than destroy them. That's the problem with this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4267605139476213511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1706769129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1706769129" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1706769129?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2006">2006</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-mature">bage-mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-horror-gothic">genre-horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-travel">genre-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=myth-folktale-fable">myth-folktale-fable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-food">sub-food</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-dreams">sub-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-trees-forest">sub-trees-forest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-flying">sub-flying</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706769129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7226940499775135672">This is Stephen's spin on Zombies. These things are Zombie like, but they aren't really zombies. These things seem to still be alive, needing food, not just brains and if you cut them, they will still bleed. Yet, they no longer think and they are fairly mindless, like a zombie. Stephen riffs off zombies.<br/><br/>I found this book entertaining and I didn't want to put the story down. Stephen is amazing at writing characters and I was drawn in by Clay, Tom and Alice. We meet them in the heart of Boston whe</span>
  <span id="freeText7226940499775135672" style="display:none">This is Stephen's spin on Zombies. These things are Zombie like, but they aren't really zombies. These things seem to still be alive, needing food, not just brains and if you cut them, they will still bleed. Yet, they no longer think and they are fairly mindless, like a zombie. Stephen riffs off zombies.<br /><br />I found this book entertaining and I didn't want to put the story down. Stephen is amazing at writing characters and I was drawn in by Clay, Tom and Alice. We meet them in the heart of Boston when the pulse goes out and the world gets extremely crazy. There was blood and gore and violence in this book, but I have to say, I was expecting a lot more and there could have been more. <br /><br />The people who didn't use their phones had to figure out what happened and the new rules of the game:<br /><br />Rule 1: don't use a cell phone<br />Rule 2: Zombies sleep at night or they go away and so the night is safe and the day is dangerous<br />rule 3: these zombies flock like birds<br /><br />I want to talk more about the plot, so I'm going to get Spoilery.<br /><br /><br />Spoiler Warning:<br /><br /><br /><br />The main bad zombie comes toward the middle of the book when they are in New Hampshire. The gang finds their way to an Academy and they find out what the zombies do at night, they reset and look like they are sleeping. Clay helps to move some gas tankers in the middle of their sleep quarters and they blow up around 1,000 of them. They get less blood thirsty and they evolve. They are telepathic and communicate through dreams and speaking to your mind or they can take over your body. They can also fly. Yes, Flying zombies. <br /><br />How the zombies were defeated was a solid ending, but the last chapter was a downer. He leaves the ending on a cliff-hanger, or with no answers given, which, I don't mind that device when used sparingly, but Clay has a kid and the kid was up in Maine when the pulse happens, so he is looking for the kid the whole book. The kid was turned to a zombie. The gang blows up the zombies at the climax and Clay hopes his son wasn't there. Clay goes looking for his kid and his kid isn't dead, of course. I think the book would have been more clean and bold if he didn't find his kid and meet up with Tom at the end. I don't like the fact that he was able to find the kid. It feels too neat somehow for this book. It made for a weak finish to the story, in my opinion. It seemed like a fairytale.<br /><br />I thought this was middle of the pack as far as Stephen King books go. This was an engaging read and I enjoyed my experience reading this, but it's not one of his best either. It's right in the middle of the pack. <br /><br />It certainly conveys how society walks such a thin rope of functioning and anarchy. It does make one think. It's apocalyptic. Now, I need to see the movie. Take away: be wary of technology. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7226940499775135672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_600511124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600511124" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600511124?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">King completionists</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600511124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5866183899215882028">Five stars for the first half. One star for the last 200 pages, wherein King drags his ass like a dog infested with roundworms. <br/><br/><i>Cell</i> is a five-star read all the way up to the halfway mark. You got crazies running around, <i>nom nom nomming</i> on tender bits, and a likable crew of misfits trying to stay alive. Underneath it all, King is stoking the fires of 9/11, trying to keep the fear alive a full five years after the towers fell in a half-ass attempt to scare you with real-world issues. The Phonies </span>
  <span id="freeText5866183899215882028" style="display:none">Five stars for the first half. One star for the last 200 pages, wherein King drags his ass like a dog infested with roundworms. <br /><br /><i>Cell</i> is a five-star read all the way up to the halfway mark. You got crazies running around, <i>nom nom nomming</i> on tender bits, and a likable crew of misfits trying to stay alive. Underneath it all, King is stoking the fires of 9/11, trying to keep the fear alive a full five years after the towers fell in a half-ass attempt to scare you with real-world issues. The Phonies (I do not type that word with a straight face) speak in a garbled, almost-arabic language. Slap turbans on King's version of zombies and you have a strong argument for racist propaganda. Did King do this on purpose? Mayhap he did. Mayhap he didn't. Either way, 'MURICA!<br /><br />There's this climax that takes place around midway through the book. King shits the bed after that. What action you do find on the downhill side of this novel is tired, rehashed bullshit from the first half of the book. It's honestly like reading two different books. King even repeats the big scene in the middle further down the road, but by then, the cool factor has disappeared. You can't have barbecue every night, friends and neighbors. It's fucking great on Friday, especially when beer's involved, but more of a pain in the ass on Saturday because you're still hungover from the night before and that goddamn grill is making you sweat pure ethanol.<br /><br />This is either my second or third read through of <i>Cell</i>. Can't remember, but it's certainly not my first. Because of this, I let Campbell Scott read it to me. He does a fine job at the narration, but the production quality is iffy at times. Sounds levels are fucked. He'll be really low one minute (not whispering, just low) and then he'll be loud (not yelling, just loud). Sometimes, the tone of his narration changes, as if he's started reading as another character. I still don't think this is his fault. I think it's the quality of the recording, which, in my honest opinion, is utter dogshit.<br /><br />Before we hit the Conspiracy Theory section of our program, I must say that I firmly believe King got in way over his head with this book. There's a reason why <i>The Stand</i> is 1200-pages long and <i>Cell</i> is only 450. Maybe <i>Cell</i> started as a short story or a novella and it just kept on going, or maybe he always meant for it to end the way it did. Either way, the final product makes it seem as if King just got tired of writing this particular book and stopped. I can dig open endings, but to follow Clay on his hunt only to receive the ending we get here... I don't know, man, that's kind of a dick move. Oh well, it's Uncle Stevie. Whatcha gon' do, right?<br /><br />Here there be spoilers for all of King's books. Only click on "view spoiler" if you've read through King's entire catalog. I take no responsibility for your sadness and despair at having something spoiled because you can't take instruction, ya muppet.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Obvious Tie Ins: <br /><br />Charlie the Choo Choo (the Dark Tower series)<br />The Dark Wanderer comic (obvious nods to the Dark Tower universe, especially since they are graphic novels and this came out around the time MARVEL started working on their DT comics)<br /><br />Conspiracy theory: I believe this version of the King-verse is another beam altogether from the beam of the Bear and Turtle. <i>The Stand</i> happens on one beam, as witnessed in <i>Wizard and Glass</i>, and <i>Cell</i> on another. This is how you can have two end-of-the-world scenarios in one universe.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In summation: I was hoping the sudden stop at the end would be eased by the knowledge of what was to come, but it didn't happen. <i>Cell</i> is still a three-star read and I'm sure it will remain that way for all my days. Especially since I see no reason for me to ever read this again. This one is fine for a first read through, as the ending can be a little shocking in a "Wait... what???" kind of way, but the novel definitely doesn't withstand the test of time, nor does it withstand a second read through.<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Only slightly better than AT&amp;T.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5866183899215882028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113632420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1798641851507478035">While this isn’t one of my top favourite King books, it is a thoroughly enjoyable read nonetheless! I find it’s one of those candy reads, it’s easy and entertaining and doesn’t require you to think too deeply. I like the whole idea, I really enjoyed seeing King’s spin on zombies! What made me enjoy it less than other King stories is that I didn’t fall in love with any of the characters. I did enjoy them but nothing about them really spoke to me and the story left me wanting more on that level.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1815781639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815781639" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36511432-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489446997p2/36511432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1815781639?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/36511432-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<div id="review_1821449145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1821449145" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1821449145?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780340921449" href="/book/show/1041565.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821449145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer207326315595098046">"What Darwin was too polite to say, my friends, is that we came to rule the earth not because we were the smartest, or even the meanest, but because we have always been the craziest, most murderous motherfuckers in the jungle."<br/><br/>Cell is an apocalyptic tale about mobile phones that wipe the user's brain, getting rid of any humanity and leaving behind only aggressive and destructive impulses. The story focuses on the main character, Clay, who is on a mission to find his estranged wife and son. Now l</span>
  <span id="freeText207326315595098046" style="display:none">"What Darwin was too polite to say, my friends, is that we came to rule the earth not because we were the smartest, or even the meanest, but because we have always been the craziest, most murderous motherfuckers in the jungle."<br /><br />Cell is an apocalyptic tale about mobile phones that wipe the user's brain, getting rid of any humanity and leaving behind only aggressive and destructive impulses. The story focuses on the main character, Clay, who is on a mission to find his estranged wife and son. Now living in a post-apocalyptic world and unable to use mobile phones for fear of becoming crazed maniacs, Clay and his group must navigate their way in an attempt to find out what has happened to his family.<br /><br />Okay, so, I actually really enjoyed this book. I loved the premise of it, and found it terrifying to even consider what it would be like if such an event occurred in real life. I loved how it was the use of mobile phones that created these crazed "zombies", especially because if something like this did happen, your first thought would be to call your loved ones to check they're okay. So I kinda loved that detail, added an extra layer to the story I thought.<br /><br />The characters were so-so. Clay was fine, but I think I actually preferred Tom. I also really liked Alice, so I wasn't overly happy with her storyline. The "zombies" or "phonies" as they were called in the book were downright horrifying! I really liked their behaviours and how they were used within the story. The fact that they were only active during the day and then "rebooted" at night. It felt like a unique portrayal of zombies.<br /><br />I thought the story moved at a great pace, especially at the beginning. It was non-stop terrifying. The pace did slow down a bit, particularly towards the end, but I was still very much interested and eager to see how it all panned out. But then that ending. THAT GODDAMN ENDING. Left me feeling so infuriated and angry. I absolutely hate endings like that...I was so annoyed by it that I felt like deducting a star, but then maybe in hindsight I will look back and like the ending (similar to how I feel about The Sopranos), so it can keep the star... for now. I thought it was a great read (apart from the ending) and very much underrated in the Stephen King universe. <br /><br />If I ever meet Sai King I will slap him across the face for that ending......but then hug him and declare my undying love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="207326315595098046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Yates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Yates" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates">Stefan Yates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743292337" href="/book/show/470684.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271288994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3972547398784450917">For some reason, I had seen quite a few bad reviews on Cell before I read it. Not one to usually dislike a King novel, I did go into this one without the highest of expectations and ended up being very pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/>The story centers around a mass event that turns anyone who happens to be on their cell phone at the time into a zombie. Mass chaos ensues and a small group of survivors bands together and tries to figure out what is going on and how to stop it. Some of the plot-line does have</span>
  <span id="freeText3972547398784450917" style="display:none">For some reason, I had seen quite a few bad reviews on Cell before I read it. Not one to usually dislike a King novel, I did go into this one without the highest of expectations and ended up being very pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />The story centers around a mass event that turns anyone who happens to be on their cell phone at the time into a zombie. Mass chaos ensues and a small group of survivors bands together and tries to figure out what is going on and how to stop it. Some of the plot-line does have some similarity to The Stand, but the characters are fairly unique, the dialog is good, and the action keeps rolling along at a fairly brisk pace. <br /><br />I really liked this novel. I knew that I probably would, but it was a nice surprise that it was as good as it was. I am of the opinion that not everything that Stephen King writes is destined to be a classic, but the majority of his work is well above average and I feel that one day he will be given his long overdue kudos and be placed in the literary canon with the other greats of modern literature.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_336559877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336559877" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336559877?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=braaains">braaains</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336559877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9000422293683500432">Stephen King does zombies! Well...kind of. We'll get to that in a bit.<br/><br/>But first, here's how I think this book came about:<br/><br/><i>Way back in aught-6 (2006), or just before because Cell was published in '06, but who knows with King, am I right? But anyway, we've come a long way since that time. Everyone was getting cell phones and they were just about getting to every last person around. I imagine him having this conversation with, let's say, his son, Joe Hill.</i><br/><br/><b>Stephen:</b> "Wow, cell phones have really gotte</span>
  <span id="freeText9000422293683500432" style="display:none">Stephen King does zombies! Well...kind of. We'll get to that in a bit.<br /><br />But first, here's how I think this book came about:<br /><br /><i>Way back in aught-6 (2006), or just before because Cell was published in '06, but who knows with King, am I right? But anyway, we've come a long way since that time. Everyone was getting cell phones and they were just about getting to every last person around. I imagine him having this conversation with, let's say, his son, Joe Hill.</i><br /><br /><b>Stephen:</b> "Wow, cell phones have really gotten popular lately. Everyone seems to have one."<br /><br /><b>Joe:</b> "Yeah Dad, come on, get with the times already, man." <br /><br /><b>Stephen:</b> "Well, at least we'll never get rid of these landlines right? Both are VERY necessary. [useless joke probably not in King's character, just wanted to make fun of how we used to still had landlines when everyone was switching to cell phones]<br /><br />"But seriously, I am SO sick of people being on their cell phones all the time. You can't even have an honest-to-goodness conversation with a person without someone bombarding you with a call.<br /><br />"Can't we just have real conversations with human beings anymore? Instead, we talk to electronics and let them control everything we do, sacrificing our humanity.<br /><br />"If only there was a way to put an end to this nonsense...I've got it!"<br /><br />Cell starts out as your basic zombie book. People are going about their normal business when suddenly lots of people start going crazy and attacking other people while a few people escape unscathed for a while until they get attacked.<br /><br />Well, Stephen King made a couple of changes to the normal zombie mythos (I think we can call it mythos now). Here, the zombies are created by a pulse that occurs through cell phones. All the people using their cell phones at the time of the "pulse" (as its known throughout the book) are immediately changed into what is essentially a zombie. Those without cell phones or not on them at the time are saved.<br /><br />It's not exactly clear whether they are (or have to be) dead or not, some are, but not all, but they all have the same traits, which are pretty zombie-like. They go crazy, they attack people including their own kind, and make survival the number one priority for those who weren't turned.<br /><br />They are known throughout the book not at zombies, but as "phone crazies." Boy did I hate that term after a while. It's just so dumb. It's also descriptively appropriate, but meh. Call them walkers, call them phoners even, but "phone crazies" just bugged me to no end.<br /><br />In addition, the zombies only come out during the day and therefore leave the night to the survivors.<br /><br />Cell follows Clayton Riddell, a survivor of the pulse who happened to be in Boston at the time of the "pulse." He lives in (you guessed it) Maine (but he's not a writer, he's a comic artist, completely different), which is where his family is located at the time of the pulse and provides the impetus for Clay and his group of survivors to head north.<br /><br />I did enjoy this book, but to talk about why I didn't enjoy it enough to even reach the 4 star threshold, I'm gonna have to get into some <b>spoilers</b>. These aren't huge, ruin-the-book spoilers, just possibly ruin a part of the first 200 pages/quarter of the book. You've been warned.<br /><br />/Begin mild spoilers<br /><br />I could go more into Clay's group because they do play a large role in the novel, but I just don't have the time nor the energy at the moment. Know they're there and they are some great characters.<br /><br />The reason I wasn't a huge fan of this particular zombie book is that King almost immediately kills the whole reason I read zombie books. I read them for the constant suspense and scare that the people we've grown close to are going to get eaten, turned, die, whatever.<br /><br />King introduces telepathy into the zombie mythos. <br /><br />While it's an interesting and unique take, I realized toward the end that it pretty much killed this particular zombie novel for me.<br /><br />Because the zombie apocalypse occurred through the pulse, the phone crazies (bleh) are connected somehow, they can even communicate in a way telepathically. It begins through large gatherings where they sleep during the night while getting essentially reprogrammed telepathically.<br /><br />While they are communicating telepathically, they begin to flock just like some types of animals (birds in a "v" for instance). While they flock, they don't attack humans. It just stops.<br /><br />There's more that happens and they do begin to do some much more devious things, but the survivors, and especially our little crew we follow, are essentially immune from the day-to-day zombie attack.<br /><br />Bigger Spoiler, for the novel <b>I Am Legend</b> as well: While I'm still within the spoiler section of my review, I also wanted to add that I totally thought he was going to go I Am Legend with the zombies, making the zombies the new society and the survivors the outcasts. It seemed to be going there, but didn't in the end.<br /><br />/end spoilers<br /><br />I enjoyed this book, it had great characters (as expected) and a good enough story to keep me enjoying it. It also had an interesting take on zombies that, while I applaud King for his creativity and boldness, kind of killed the zombie part of this zombie novel.<br /><br />3 out of 5 Stars (Recommended with reservations)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9000422293683500432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

From there the story gets progressively scarier and weirder. <br/>Really good story and I have another reason to not talk on a cell. (Texting only) </span>

<div id="review_3021333475" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3021333475" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3021333475?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743292337" href="/book/show/470684.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3021333475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13959865811784751416"><b>"These people are popping up everywhere. Some only commit suicide. Many others attack."</b><br/> <br/>King's foray into the zombie novel features a more traditionally defined zombie: a <u>living</u> person who is given a command, and then becomes a mindless, er, well . . . zombie. No flesh-eating here - King's zombies prefer veggies and Twinkies. And what, pray tell, is the command that turned them into violence prone fans of elevator music? Why, a little message sent on their cell phones, that's what.<br/><br/><b>"It was the ce</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13959865811784751416" style="display:none"><b>"These people are popping up everywhere. Some only commit suicide. Many others attack."</b><br /> <br />King's foray into the zombie novel features a more traditionally defined zombie: a <u>living</u> person who is given a command, and then becomes a mindless, er, well . . . zombie. No flesh-eating here - King's zombies prefer veggies and Twinkies. And what, pray tell, is the command that turned them into violence prone fans of elevator music? Why, a little message sent on their cell phones, that's what.<br /><br /><b>"It was the cell phones," she said in that same whisper. "It was the cell phones, all right."</b><br /> <br />Originally published in 2006, (just look at that state-of-the-art flip-phone on the cover), there were many "normies" who did not have cellular phones, and therefore avoided the dreaded conversion. Nowadays, the survivors would be far fewer in number as there's almost no one without a cell phone. Heck, even the Amish women who come into the library are clutching the things. <br /> <br />I will say that while this one held my interest, I was not terrified, or even mildly frightened. Perhaps it was the characters - bland, and not particularly inspiring. Or maybe it's that the tale seems to have originated as a short story, and was stretched beyond its capacity to novel length. But I think the most likely reason of all is that if you've read more than a few King books, you've essentially read this <s>retread</s> one: there was nothing special about it, nothing memorable. <br /> <br />An okay read, but not one of the man's best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13959865811784751416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586261569" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586261569?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781419385384" href="/book/show/3062532-cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586261569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5034815784772371610"><br/><br/>Yay! Another successful King re-read! <br/><br/>I read Cell when it first came out and I loved it. I’ve wanted to do a reread since hearing the whispers about the movie production. All I needed to hear was John Cusack and I knew it would be gold. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462381036ra/18990681.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I mean, seriously. The guy has to be one of the most underrated actors ever.<br/><br/>Then came the announcement of Samuel L. Jackson joining the cast and I removed any doubt from my mind. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462381036ra/18990682.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>SOLD.<br/><br/>Clay Riddell has just sold his first comic. He’s about to make a shit-load of c</span>
  <span id="freeText5034815784772371610" style="display:none"><br><br>Yay! Another successful King re-read! <br><br>I read Cell when it first came out and I loved it. I’ve wanted to do a reread since hearing the whispers about the movie production. All I needed to hear was John Cusack and I knew it would be gold. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462381036ra/18990681.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, seriously. The guy has to be one of the most underrated actors ever.<br><br>Then came the announcement of Samuel L. Jackson joining the cast and I removed any doubt from my mind. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462381036ra/18990682.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>SOLD.<br><br>Clay Riddell has just sold his first comic. He’s about to make a shit-load of cash. He’s excited. He can’t wait to tell his son- and even kind of his estranged wifey. There he is basking in all the glory of his success when <b>the Pulse</b> occurs. Any person on their phone at the time of the Pulse goes completely insane.<br><br>They kill themselves or others in violent and vicious ways. One guy even bites the ear off a dog. Another girl smashes her own face repeatedly off of a pole until she dies. It’s fucking awesome. I know people say this is King’s version of zombies but I disagree. I think the Pulse strips you down to your most primal self. You become a beast; an animal. <br><br><b> At bottom, you see, we are not Homo sapiens as all. Our core is madness. The prime directive is murder. What Darwin was too polite to say, my friends, is that we came to rule the earth not because we were the smartest, or even the meanest, but because we have always been the craziest, most murderous motherfuckers in the jungle. And that is what the Pulse exposed five days ago.</b><br><br>The pace of the book does slow down but the story does not. It develops into a one-of-a-kind mindfuck of a tale. <br><br>While I love the opening sequence for its relentless violence, I think the ending is my favorite part. King nailed it. His endings are sooooooooooo hit and miss among his fans-at least in my experience- it is nice to see an ending I can really appreciate. I think it was the perfect ending for this book. <br><br>If you haven’t had a chance to read it yet- I strongly recommend it. If you have- make sure you check out the trailer for the movie! It looks amazing! You can check that out <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0775440/?ref_=fn_al_tt_1" rel="nofollow noopener">right here</a><br><br>Ps. The docked star is mostly due to the inconsistent narration of the audio book. It was patchy and you could clearly hear the edits. It was enough to take me out of the story. <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5034815784772371610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText6052661471331737834" style="display:none">I read this novel when it first came out, and was too annoyed by the ending to read it again. Well we saw the movie (with John Cryer and Samuel L. Jackson) and I wanted to see if the movie was much like the novel. It was, for the most part. And IMDb tells us why Stephen King changed the ending to the movie (as he wrote the screenplay as well), in the trivia section. (Fans).<br /><br />So Campbell Scott is the narrator of the audiobook, and I loved his rendition of this novel. He’s great, and should be used much more by Simon &amp; Schuster Audio.<br />My love for King’s writing will never diminish, and my rating for this novel stays the same. Yes, even though we have no idea what happens next. <br /><br />4 stars, and recommended.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne Barrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne Barrett" href="/user/show/21372390-wayne-barrett">Wayne Barrett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743292337" href="/book/show/470684.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459156971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15533503911575176053"><br/>4.5<br/><br/>Once again Mr. King shows why he is a master. I wouldn't rank this one among his best, but that is because he has done so many masterpieces that it is hard to compete. But I still thought this was a great book. <br/><br/>King used some basic concepts; cell phone usage, zombies, and yet he presented a tale that was unique and creative. This one was short compared to his average novels and because of his entertaining, free-flowing script, this was another one of those books that was a breeze to read. <br/><br/>I c</span>
  <span id="freeText15533503911575176053" style="display:none"><br />4.5<br /><br />Once again Mr. King shows why he is a master. I wouldn't rank this one among his best, but that is because he has done so many masterpieces that it is hard to compete. But I still thought this was a great book. <br /><br />King used some basic concepts; cell phone usage, zombies, and yet he presented a tale that was unique and creative. This one was short compared to his average novels and because of his entertaining, free-flowing script, this was another one of those books that was a breeze to read. <br /><br />I can see where some people might scrutinize the ending, but I like the way the author left us with a myriad of possibilities and the opportunity to use our own imaginations to conclude the story. </span>

<div id="review_1428452261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428452261" />
    <a title="PUMPKINHEAD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24008361-pumpkinhead"><img alt="PUMPKINHEAD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516591879p2/24008361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1428452261?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PUMPKINHEAD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PUMPKINHEAD" href="/user/show/24008361-pumpkinhead">PUMPKINHEAD</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=not-what-i-hoped">not-what-i-hoped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24008361-pumpkinhead?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428452261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9977359034150730187">My overall feelings on this book? Meh... but in a good way. <br/><br/>I'm a huge Stephen King fan, but I think I'm going to start defining my adoration for him by a certain era. I find I love his earlier stuff, but don't particularly love (or sometimes even like) his later stuff. 'Cell' is a good example of how a former master of horror has now become a much more average author. <br/><br/>Now, this is not a bad novel. It varies from alright to good, rarely achieving greatness, but scoring points for story, some pac</span>
  <span id="freeText9977359034150730187" style="display:none">My overall feelings on this book? Meh... but in a good way. <br /><br />I'm a huge Stephen King fan, but I think I'm going to start defining my adoration for him by a certain era. I find I love his earlier stuff, but don't particularly love (or sometimes even like) his later stuff. 'Cell' is a good example of how a former master of horror has now become a much more average author. <br /><br />Now, this is not a bad novel. It varies from alright to good, rarely achieving greatness, but scoring points for story, some pace, and King's usual habit of giving us the creeps. But the story was part of the problem too. Although there was a slight twist on the 'Zombie tale' (people become zombie-ish creatures after receiving a signal through their cell phones), this novel quickly turns into a story we've all heard before: The majority of people become zombies, small groups of living people escape/fight to stay alive in the ensuing zombie apocalypse. <br /><br />Been there. Done that. Many times. And it's played out. <br /><br />But there was a little bit of new life breathed into an old trope, and it was as decent as the next good book about the undead. Still, I expected a lot more from our crowned ruler of creepy books. It's a bit annoying and disheartening when someone like Stephen King starts becoming an imitator instead of an originator, or when it feels like big-time authors are getting lazy in light of their success (I have the same feeling about authors Peter Straub and Dean Koontz).<br /><br />I read a book like 'Cell' and I can't help wonder if maybe it is time we had a new 'King' of horror fiction. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9977359034150730187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_95803081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95803081" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1254714-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513279210p2/1254714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95803081?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/1254714-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1254714-steve?shelf=horror-and-dark-fiction">horror-and-dark-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1254714-steve?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95803081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10408769011083320273">There have been many who have compared Stephen King's <i>Cell</i> with his earlier Apocalypse-Now effort, <i>The Stand</i>. And there are some good reasons, End-of-the-World setting, the survivors polarized into two camps, one camp, arguably no longer even human, a big bang ending in an arena like setting, etc. But there are differences as well. When King wrote <i>The Stand</i>, it seemed to mark a moment in that writer's life where he was becoming overt in things religious. <i>The Stand</i> is a battle between good and ev</span>
  <span id="freeText10408769011083320273" style="display:none">There have been many who have compared Stephen King's <i>Cell</i> with his earlier Apocalypse-Now effort, <i>The Stand</i>. And there are some good reasons, End-of-the-World setting, the survivors polarized into two camps, one camp, arguably no longer even human, a big bang ending in an arena like setting, etc. But there are differences as well. When King wrote <i>The Stand</i>, it seemed to mark a moment in that writer's life where he was becoming overt in things religious. <i>The Stand</i> is a battle between good and evil, darkness and light, King's Book of Revelation if you will. <i>Cell</i> is more ambiguous. The zombie like creatures that inhabit the novel are, through no fault of their own, zapped by the "surge," which pretty much wipes out anyone's human hard drive if they happened to own and use a cell phone. No choice there. To some extent, as animal like as they can be, the zombies of <i>Cell</i> are pitiable. Meanwhile, King's little band of survivors are just trying to get somewhere, find some human traction in a world that has been blasted. In particular, there is Clay Riddell, who in his previous pre-Surge life was a graphic artist, and probably something of dreamer. His marriage is probably on the rocks, but he loves his son dearly, and when the deal goes down, he can only think of one thing: to get to him. In King's universe, we now see the Manichean Good and Evil from the <i>Stand</i> being replaced by <i>Cell's</i> Love and Duty. To some extent <i>Cell</i> is similar to Cormac McCarthy's <i>The Road</i>. Both are Father and Son stories; both look beyond the End, to what must remain if we are to survive as a species: Hope. The ending of <i>Cell</i> has bothered some, but I think this is unwarranted. In many ways, it's one of King's most powerful endings, and shows the mature writer that he has become. There is no need for a sequel, and I would be surprised if King wrote one. <br /><br /><i>Cell</i> is a fine effort by King, and one that will be viewed, as time goes by, as one of his best efforts. It has as an effective leanness and nastiness to it that will remind some of <i>Thinner</i>, but also a suggestive depth to it that carries it beyond merely Pulp Fiction. <br /><br />* Note: I think King totally ripped off Simon Clark's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/906024.Blood_Crazy" title="Blood Crazy by Simon Clark" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Crazy</a>. I still like what King did with it, but I'm dropping a star (from 4 to 3) as a result. Comparing the two, I also think Clark had the better story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10408769011083320273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_14145822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14145822" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858949-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14145822?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/858949-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743292337" href="/book/show/470684.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=apocolypse">apocolypse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14145822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5467334591175989298">You know, I'm pretty sure he said he was retiring a few years ago. Not that I'm complaining, mind you - this was a fun read. I just figure we should never trust a writer when they say they're done. This is like crack to them, I suppose.<br/><br/>With this book, King is back to my favorite story type of his - world-spanning apocalypse. Ain't nothing better than the end of the world, in my judgment, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand__The_Complete___Unabridged_Edition_' title='The Stand (The Complete & Unabridged Edition) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Stand</a> is still one of my favorite King books.<br/><br/>In this one, though, he takes a slightly different appro</span>
  <span id="freeText5467334591175989298" style="display:none">You know, I'm pretty sure he said he was retiring a few years ago. Not that I'm complaining, mind you - this was a fun read. I just figure we should never trust a writer when they say they're done. This is like crack to them, I suppose.<br /><br />With this book, King is back to my favorite story type of his - world-spanning apocalypse. Ain't nothing better than the end of the world, in my judgment, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand__The_Complete___Unabridged_Edition_" title="The Stand (The Complete &amp; Unabridged Edition) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stand</a> is still one of my favorite King books.<br /><br />In this one, though, he takes a slightly different approach. In <i>The Stand</i>, the full scale of the disaster is revealed in pieces, with tantalizing peeks at how bad Captain Trips is every now and then until we finally see just what it means to lose 99.6% of the population in ten days. Hint: stinky.<br /><br />For <i>Cell</i>, King tells us right up front, before the first page of the story, that the world as we know it would be gone in two weeks. Then he gives us a happy, almost exuberant main character, whose life has just taken a massive turn for the better and who believes he can see a bright and shining future ahead of him.<br /><br />A few pages later, of course, The Pulse hits. And the world, for all intents and purposes, ends. At 3:03 PM EST, October 1st, everyone who uses a cell phone goes instantly and ferally insane. The people who see the first waves of chaos do the natural thing - pick up their cell phones to find out what's happening. And in an instant, they are part of the madness.<br /><br />It's a terrible new world, to say the least. And Clayton Riddell has to make his way to his wife and son, hoping that they survived the pulse and the murderous madness that followed.<br /><br />The story is not, technically, original. King borrows a great deal from other writers and artists - he thanks <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8726.Richard_Matheson" title="Richard Matheson" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Matheson</a> and George Romero up front, as well he should. And he has one of the main characters refer to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/545.Neal_Stephenson" title="Neal Stephenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Neal Stephenson</a> as "a God," perhaps to balance against criticism of apparent similarities with Snow Crash. And, of course, because Stephenson is a god, if a terribly difficult one to understand all the time....<br /><br />Of course, he can't escape comparisons to his original apocalypse book, <i>The Stand</i>, but he didn't reference it directly. The characters seem to have a more difficult time getting their way in this book, it seems, and they certainly cover less ground. And they're not, to my mind, as memorable as the wonderful cast of characters who wandered through The Stand. No Randall Flagg, either.<br /><br />However, for you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43615.The_Gunslinger__The_Dark_Tower__Book_1_" title="The Gunslinger (The Dark Tower, Book 1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Tower</a> fans, there's one oblique reference in this book: It's in the "Kashwak" section, just at the end of part 15, pretty close to the end of the book. You should know it when you see it.<br /><br />Speaking of which.... I haven't read everything King's written since he finished out <i>Dark Tower</i>, but it looks like he's decided that closure is overrated. That's all I'm gonna say about that. It's not a bad ending by any stretch, it's just.... *sigh*<br /><br />Anyway, pick it up. Fun book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5467334591175989298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_963895531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/963895531" />
    <a title="Stylo Fantome" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32061247-stylo-fantome"><img alt="Stylo Fantome" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555440753p2/32061247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/963895531?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stylo Fantome" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stylo Fantome" href="/user/show/32061247-stylo-fantome">Stylo Fantome</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer963895531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13799162000256492046">I am actually not the biggest Stephen King fan. I went through a kick where some of my favorite old-ish movies, I was going back and reading the books they had been made from - Jaws, The Exorcist, Silence of the Lambs. So of course, I wound up hunting down quite a few Stephen King books.<br/><br/>I kept seeing this book on the shelf at the library, and the blurb intrigued me, so finally I checked it out and read it.<br/><br/>I really, really liked it! I am a fan of apocalypse/zombie themes, movies, whatevs, and thi</span>
  <span id="freeText13799162000256492046" style="display:none">I am actually not the biggest Stephen King fan. I went through a kick where some of my favorite old-ish movies, I was going back and reading the books they had been made from - Jaws, The Exorcist, Silence of the Lambs. So of course, I wound up hunting down quite a few Stephen King books.<br /><br />I kept seeing this book on the shelf at the library, and the blurb intrigued me, so finally I checked it out and read it.<br /><br />I really, really liked it! I am a fan of apocalypse/zombie themes, movies, whatevs, and this book is strong with both of those. Of course, there aren't zombies in this book - they are living, breathing human beings. Just ..., changed. Evolved. Different.<br /><br />This book was haunting. There is no denying that very few authors can give you the heebie jeebies as well as Stephen King, and this book is no exception. When the shiz starts hitting the fan, the pandemonium that's described is scary as all get out. The second time I read it, it was late at night and I was in bed downstairs alone. Unbeknownst to me, the teenage neighbors at the end of the street had decided to throw a kegger that turned into a Fight Club. Needless to say, I nearly peed myself as the noise outside seemed to mirror the noise in the book.<br /><br />Like many Stephen King books, this follows a man going through an unusual, terrifying situation, trying to get back to his family and life, and forming friends and allies and foes along the way. A phone call causes everyone who answered their phone to go insane. Our hero didn't have a phone, thankfully. At first, it's a murderous rampage free for all. Then the phone-zombies calm down a little and start to mass together.<br /><br />Never a good sign.<br /><br />Throw in some psychic abilities and a strong telepath, a frightening red sweater, and lots of guns that never really do anything but hurt the ones trying to use them, and you've got an interesting story.<br /><br />I was very excited when I saw that this was being made into a movie - visions of Thomas Jane as the lead dancing through my head. Instead, last I heard John Cusack was cast to play the hero, and I just can't see that. Boo.<br /><br />If you like Stephen King, read this book. If you don't like Stephen King but like scary novels, read this book. If you don't like Stephen King AND you don't like scary novels, then I'm not sure why you're looking at this page. This book rocks. Check it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13799162000256492046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_970722950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19253213-heena-rathore-p?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>,
