        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer970722950&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer970722950" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15970251905511943682">It’s the best book I’ve read after A Song Of Ice And Fire! The characterization and the narration is incredibly amazing. It catches the reader’s interest from the first line to the very last word. Yes!<br/><br/>The story starts minutes before The Pulse occurred and takes us through the entire scenario in perfect detail. You’ll get a feeling that you are right next to the lead, Clayton Riddell and are experiencing each and everything. The craziers or the phone-crazies are easy to picture and seem scary. Cl</span>
  <span id="freeText15970251905511943682" style="display:none">It’s the best book I’ve read after A Song Of Ice And Fire! The characterization and the narration is incredibly amazing. It catches the reader’s interest from the first line to the very last word. Yes!<br /><br />The story starts minutes before The Pulse occurred and takes us through the entire scenario in perfect detail. You’ll get a feeling that you are right next to the lead, Clayton Riddell and are experiencing each and everything. The craziers or the phone-crazies are easy to picture and seem scary. Clay’s allies, Tom and Alice are perfect and the way they survive is really intriguing. The major part of the book is about Clay’s journey to save his son and that he does! Or not! Well, the best part (as far as I’m concerned) is the open-ending, which is a treat for reader’s imagination.<br /><br />One of the other things I liked about Cell is that The Pulse, that is the virus, which is also referred to as a programme, is shown to be corrupted and wormed. Which actually takes the entire concept to a whole new level.<br /><br />This book is amazing. I love it and I guess now I’ll be on a Stephen-King-reading-spree… It very well satisfied my hunger of always wanting more from any post-apocalyptic (specially Zombie) movie. From now on, I’m gonna switch to apocalyptic books instead of movies cause in movies you just get to watch stuff but in a book, specially by King you really get to feel the intensity.<br />Throughout the entire book and it’s events, I was right there with Clay and the gang and I’ll tell you what, I was so involved in the happenings of the book that yes, I did hesitate to pick up my cell when it rang!<br /><br />It’s not a book it’s an experience and I really can’t have enough of it!<br /><br />You can also read this review at <a href="http://thereadingbud.wordpress.com/2014/07/08/book-review-cell-by-stephen-king/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reading Bud</a></span>

<div id="review_839711714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839711714" />
    <a title="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28225370-sadie-hartmann-mother-horror"><img alt="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596596514p2/28225370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839711714?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" href="/user/show/28225370-sadie-hartmann-mother-horror">Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743292337" href="/book/show/470684.Cell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839711714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10394911516864175148">So this is a King re read for me. I reviewed it the first time at 4 stars and I'm deciding now, upon reading it again, to dock a star.<br/>Let's start with Clay, I like Clay as a protagonist but he's not one of King's more memorable main characters. If we were to rank him, he'd probably fall somewhere towards the middle. Kind of forgettable. I actually thought Tom would be a better main character; he had better lines.<br/>The first part of this book kicks ass! I love the opening scene in the streets when </span>
  <span id="freeText10394911516864175148" style="display:none">So this is a King re read for me. I reviewed it the first time at 4 stars and I'm deciding now, upon reading it again, to dock a star.<br />Let's start with Clay, I like Clay as a protagonist but he's not one of King's more memorable main characters. If we were to rank him, he'd probably fall somewhere towards the middle. Kind of forgettable. I actually thought Tom would be a better main character; he had better lines.<br />The first part of this book kicks ass! I love the opening scene in the streets when the Pulse hits and Clay is first hand witness to all this crazy shit going down. People screaming these crazy made up words (which I feel like I have seen before? Dark Tower junkies?) and Pixie Light and Pixie Dark tearing into each other--but then after the excitement wares off, King transitions into normalcy.<br />This is the boring part.<br />I'm sorry but it just got boring. I like Raggedy Man but I hate how the zombies begin evolving and develop supernatural powers.<br />I understand that King wanted to maybe shake up the genre a bit but it didn't work for me.<br />The last 100 pages or so leading up to the ending (DO NOT LIKE THE ENDING) was a huge disappointment. So this is why I'm docking the star from my original review.<br />Anyhow, fun re-read, especially since I knew my friend Jo in Ireland and my friend Them here in the States were reading it along with me--made me feel connected to them through good ol' SK.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10394911516864175148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2178880655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2178880655" />
    <a title="Holly Ann&amp;#x1f98b;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67375981-holly-ann-x1f98b"><img alt="Holly Ann&amp;#x1f98b;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599405911p2/67375981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2178880655?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly Ann&amp;#x1f98b;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly Ann&amp;#x1f98b;" href="/user/show/67375981-holly-ann-x1f98b">Holly Ann&amp;#x1f98b;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444707823" href="/book/show/10431822-cell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67375981-holly-ann-x1f98b?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2178880655&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2178880655" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12219614763032594150">3 Stars✨<br/><br/>My very first Stephen King book!!!!! Slightly disappointing but I’m just happy that I’ve read a Stephen King😋🙈❤️<br/><br/>I can understand now what people mean when they say “his descriptions can be lengthy and very much in detail”. However, I LOVE THAT! I don’t get enough detail in some books nowadays, and this felt like a breath of fresh air. I could really visualise where I was, which is usually so hard.<br/><br/>The beginning of the book WAS AMAZING. Honestly, so good in so many ways. The intensity didn</span>
  <span id="freeText12219614763032594150" style="display:none">3 Stars✨<br /><br />My very first Stephen King book!!!!! Slightly disappointing but I’m just happy that I’ve read a Stephen King😋🙈❤️<br /><br />I can understand now what people mean when they say “his descriptions can be lengthy and very much in detail”. However, I LOVE THAT! I don’t get enough detail in some books nowadays, and this felt like a breath of fresh air. I could really visualise where I was, which is usually so hard.<br /><br />The beginning of the book WAS AMAZING. Honestly, so good in so many ways. The intensity didn’t let up for the first half of the book and I was enthralled❤️A real page turner and it wad everything I expected from a Stephen King story. The characters are so endearing and I feel like I know them especially Tom McCourt who is, in my not so humble opinion, one of the greatest characters I’ve ever read about... EVER☺️<br /><br />........but........<br /><br />Things slow down. A lot. And I feel like. I’m walking. In tar. For the rest. Of. The book.😭<br /><br />Whilst the action seems to ramp up, the creepiness and the eerie atmosphere diminishes and I’m left reading a story that confused me and made me feel bored! By that I mean, the idea of the Crazies “evolving” was just not what I expected. Its not that it wasn’t a good idea, its that I didn’t like it😕I wanted to read about crazy folk who killed people and lots of running from them and killing them, not weird warbling idiots who are slowly turning the “normies” into “crazies”. SNOOZE FEST!<br /><br />There were shocks, and scares and tension. But there was a lot of boredom and plain confusion of ideas in Cell which disappointed me. Perhaps its my lack of experience with Stephen King, or maybe my sheer dislike at some of his ideas🤷‍♀️</span>
  <a data-text-id="12219614763032594150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lSwwEEZsFSfVWlNL0C9sJ5zIV4zhImyzAwyJ/raZKCUTXA7FbRSboXODo2xjhqax0fA0j4KGfqw8NAgaH57T9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+VQ69HKvy0c926gZYdqImDeY+rEzK3WG241X8nb+Cqd/JAQhWddFwZsCWD7Sc0IOeqCZslCPZ5nktdYW3/nxdQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,330
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11761816187873348280">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText11761816187873348280" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11761816187873348280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
